<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Eastern Europe</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="infobox geography vcard" style="width:22em;width:23em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:1.25em; white-space:nowrap"><span class="fn org">Eastern Europe</span></th>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedtoprow">
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ukraine_topo_big-1.png" title="Geographic features of Eastern Europe"><img alt="Geographic features of Eastern Europe" data-file-height="926" data-file-width="959" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ukraine_topo_big-1.png/250px-Ukraine_topo_big-1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ukraine_topo_big-1.png/375px-Ukraine_topo_big-1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ukraine_topo_big-1.png/500px-Ukraine_topo_big-1.png 2x" width="250"/></a><br/>
<small>Geographic features of Eastern Europe</small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Eastern Europe</b>, also known as <b>East Europe</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/East" title="East">eastern</a> part of the <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a>. There is no consensus on the precise area it covers, partly because the term has a wide range of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geopolitical" title="Geopolitical">geopolitical</a>, geographical, cultural, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socioeconomic" title="Socioeconomic">socioeconomic</a> connotations. There are "almost as many definitions of Eastern Europe as there are scholars of the region".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheBalkans_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheBalkans-1">[1]</a></sup> A related <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> paper adds that "every assessment of spatial identities is essentially a social and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_construct" title="Cultural construct">cultural construct</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>One definition describes Eastern Europe as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_culture" title="European culture">cultural</a> (and econo-cultural) entity: the region lying in Europe with main characteristics consisting in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Orthodox</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turco-Islamic</a> influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EasternEuropeHandbook_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-EasternEuropeHandbook-3">[3]</a></sup> Another definition was created during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and used more or less synonymously with the term <i><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a></i>. A similar definition names the formerly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">communist</a> European <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">states</a> outside the Soviet Union as Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EasternEuropeHandbook_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-EasternEuropeHandbook-3">[3]</a></sup> Historians and social scientists generally view such definitions as outdated or relegating,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sofiaecho.com_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-sofiaecho.com-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotf.edu_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-cotf.edu-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEreview_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-CEreview-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> but they are still sometimes used for statistical purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuroVoc_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-EuroVoc-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-un-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Several definitions of Eastern Europe exist today, but they often lack precision or are extremely general. These definitions vary both across cultures and among experts, even <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_scientists" title="Political scientists">political scientists</a>, recently becoming more and more imprecise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical">Geographical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geographical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_continents" title="Boundaries between continents">geographical land border</a> of the eastern edge of Europe. In the west, however, the <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious</a> boundaries of "Eastern Europe" are subject to considerable overlap and, most importantly, have undergone historical fluctuations, which make a precise definition of the western boundaries of Eastern Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_midpoint_of_Europe" title="Geographical midpoint of Europe">geographical midpoint of Europe</a> somewhat difficult.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EuroVoc">EuroVoc</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: EuroVoc">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_sub-regions_(according_to_EuroVoc,_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="917" data-file-width="1138" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png/220px-European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png/330px-European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png/440px-European_sub-regions_%28according_to_EuroVoc%2C_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_sub-regions_(according_to_EuroVoc,_the_thesaurus_of_the_EU).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
European sub-regions according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EuroVoc" title="EuroVoc">EuroVoc</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eurovoc" title="Eurovoc">Eurovoc</a>, a multilingual <a href="/wiki/Thesaurus" title="Thesaurus">thesaurus</a> maintained by the <b><a href="/wiki/Publications_Office_of_the_European_Union" title="Publications Office of the European Union">Publications Office of the European Union</a></b>, provides entries for "23 EU languages"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> (<i>Bulgarian, Croatian, Czech</i>, Danish, Dutch, English, Estonian, Finnish, French, German, Greek, <i>Hungarian</i>, Italian, Latvian, Lithuanian, Maltese, <i>Polish</i>, Portuguese, <i>Romanian, Slovak, Slovenian</i>, Spanish and Swedish) plus languages of candidate countries (<i>Albanian</i>, <i>Macedonian</i> and <i>Serbian</i>). Of these, those in italics are classified as "Eastern Europe" in this source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Other official web-pages of the European Union classify some of the above-mentioned countries as strictly Central European (Hungary, Poland, Slovakia, Czech Republic, Slovenia).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Intelligence_Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Central Intelligence Agency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastern-Europe-map2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eastern-Europe-map2.svg/220px-Eastern-Europe-map2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eastern-Europe-map2.svg/330px-Eastern-Europe-map2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eastern-Europe-map2.svg/440px-Eastern-Europe-map2.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eastern-Europe-map2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> which defines Azerbaijan, Armenia, Georgia, Kazakhstan, Russia and Turkey as primarily or entirely in Asia, and Cyprus as in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF9900; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Eastern Europe</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFBD59; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Southeastern Europe</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CE7B00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Transcontinental</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">CIA</a> defines Eastern Europe as Belarus, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, Moldova, Russia (transcontinental), Turkey (transcontinental) and Ukraine.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political.2C_military_and_economic">Political, military and economic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Political, military and economic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="509" data-file-width="812" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg/220px-Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg/330px-Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg/440px-Europe-blocs-49-89x4.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical">Historical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Historical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>One view of the present boundaries of Eastern Europe came into being during the final stages of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The area eventually came to encompass all the European countries which were under Soviet influence. Countries which had <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> governments in the postwar era (1945-1991), and <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutral</a> countries were classified by the nature of their political regimes.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> increased the number of reasons for the division of Europe into two parts along the borders of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> states. (<i>See</i>: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe#World_War_II_and_the_onset_of_the_Cold_War" title="Eastern Europe">the Cold War</a> section).</p>
<p>The economic organisation connecting the countries was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_for_Mutual_Economic_Assistance" title="Council for Mutual Economic Assistance">Council for Mutual Economic Assistance</a>.</p>
<p>This view is now generally viewed as outadated.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary">Contemporary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contemporary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After the fall of the USSR, a new boundary of Eastern Europe emerged defined by the membership in political and economic organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS), and more recently the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural">Cultural</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cultural">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cultural view excludes from the definition of Eastern Europe states historically and culturally different, constituting part of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>. This could potentially refer to various formerly communist countries of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> which have different political, religious, cultural, and economic histories from their eastern neighbors (e.g., Russia and Ukraine). (<i>See</i>: <a href="#Classical_antiquity_and_medieval_origins">Classical antiquity and medieval origins</a> section).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious">Religious</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Religious">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The East–West Schism is the break of communion and theology between what are now the Eastern (Orthodox) and Western (Roman Catholic, as well as from the 16th century also Protestant) churches which began in the 11th century and lasts until this very day. It divided Christianity in Europe, and consequently the world, into <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern Christianity</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_developments">Contemporary developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Contemporary developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">fall of the Iron Curtain</a> brought the end of the East–West division in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> but this geopolitical concept is sometimes still used for quick reference by the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltic_states">Baltic states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Baltic states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a></div>
<p>Some sources<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> place the Baltic states in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a> whereas the CIA World Factbook places the region in Eastern Europe.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transcaucasia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> nations of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> are included in <a href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_continents" title="Boundaries between continents">definitions of Eastern Europe</a> and/or histories of Eastern Europe. They are located in the transition zone of Eastern Europe and <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. They participate in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> program, and are members of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, which specifies that all three are <i>geographically</i> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> but have <i>political</i> and cultural connections to Turkey and Europe. Georgia has sought membership in NATO and the European Union.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Factbook" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic Society</a> atlases, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>, have always listed and/or shown the three states within Asia. As with the Baltic states, the Transcaucasian nations differ somewhat, with <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> culturally oriented more toward Eastern Europe, and <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shiite Muslim</a> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> culturally oriented more toward the Asian <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a></li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">Disputed states</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Abkhazia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="1080" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nagorno-Karabakh.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">Nagorno-Karabakh Republic</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/46px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_former_Soviet_states">Other former Soviet states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other former Soviet states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_States" title="Post-Soviet States">Post-Soviet States</a></div>
<p>Several other former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> republics may be considered part of Eastern Europe</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> is a transcontinental country where the <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">Western part</a> is in Eastern Europe and the rest is in Asia.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> is a transcontinental country, predominantly in Asia, with a relatively small section in Europe.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="900" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/46px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Moldova.svg/23px-Flag_of_Moldova.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Moldova.svg/35px-Flag_of_Moldova.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Moldova.svg/46px-Flag_of_Moldova.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a></li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">Disputed states</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1400" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Flag_of_Transnistria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Transnistria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Flag_of_Transnistria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Transnistria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Flag_of_Transnistria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Transnistria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Europe">Central Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Central Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a></div>
<p>The term "Central Europe" is often used by historians to designate states formerly belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, including parts of modern-day Belarus and Ukraine. "Central Europe" thus overlaps with "Eastern Europe." The following countries are labeled Eastern European by some commentators and as Central European by others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wallace_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-wallace-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huntington_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-huntington-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1280" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Flag_of_Slovakia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Slovakia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> (most often placed in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> but sometimes in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Armstrong2007_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Armstrong2007-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeastern_Europe">Southeastern Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Southeastern Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a></div>
<p>Most Southeastern European states did not belong to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> (save Bulgaria, Romania, and for a short time, Albania) although some of them were represented in the <a href="/wiki/Cominform" title="Cominform">Cominform</a>. Only some of them can be included in the classical former political definition of Eastern Europe. Some can be considered part of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-un-10">[10]</a></sup> However, most can be characterized as belonging to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South-eastern_Europe" title="South-eastern Europe">South-eastern Europe</a>, but some of them may also be included in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> or Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="700" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/21px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/32px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Flag_of_Albania.svg/42px-Flag_of_Albania.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> belongs to Southeastern Europe.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> is in the central part of the Balkans; geographically belongs to Southern/Southeastern Europe and sometimes included in the North-Eastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>, but can also be included in Eastern Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> is geographically situated in the eastern Mediterranean, off the coast of west Asian mainland, however due to its political, cultural, and historical ties to Europe, it is often regarded as part of Southern, and Southeastern Europe.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/23px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/35px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Greece.svg/45px-Flag_of_Greece.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> is a rather unusual case and may be included, variously, in Western,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Southeastern<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> or Southern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indexmundi_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-indexmundi-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un2_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-un2-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1400" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Flag_of_Macedonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Macedonia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> belongs to Southeastern Europe.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="640" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/23px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/35px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Flag_of_Montenegro.svg/46px-Flag_of_Montenegro.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> belongs to Southeastern Europe.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> can be included in Eastern Europe in the Cold War context, but is commonly referred to as belonging to Southeastern Europe<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eia.doe.gov_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-eia.doe.gov-40">[40]</a></sup> or Central Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> is included in notions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> lies partially in Southeastern Europe: only the region known as <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a>, which constitutes 3% of the country's total land mass, lies west of the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">Disputed states</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="840" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/21px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/32px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Flag_of_Kosovo.svg/42px-Flag_of_Kosovo.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> belongs to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="1026" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">Northern Cyprus</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity_and_medieval_origins">Classical antiquity and medieval origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Classical antiquity and medieval origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caucasus" title="History of the Caucasus">History of the Caucasus</a></div>
<p>Ancient kingdoms of the region included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orontid_Armenia" title="Orontid Armenia">Orontid Armenia</a> <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">Colchis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caucasian_Iberia" title="Caucasian Iberia">Iberia</a>. These kingdoms were either from the start, or later on incorporated into various Iranian empires, including the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persian" title="Sassanid Persian">Sassanid Persian</a> Empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rapp_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rapp-42">[42]</a></sup> Parts of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and more northern areas were ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Persians</a> as well, including <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)" title="Paeonia (kingdom)">Paeonia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedon" title="Macedon">Macedon</a>, and most of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coastal regions of <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Owing to the rivalry between <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Rome</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantium</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persians" title="Sassanid Persians">Sassanid Persians</a>, the former would invade the region several times, although it was never able to hold the region, unlike the Sassanids who ruled over most of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> during their entire rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earliest known distinctions between east and west in Europe originate in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. As the Roman domain expanded, a cultural and linguistic division appeared between the mainly <a href="/wiki/Koine_Greek" title="Koine Greek">Greek</a>-speaking eastern provinces which had formed the highly urbanized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">Hellenistic civilization</a>. In contrast the western territories largely adopted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin language</a>. This cultural and linguistic division was eventually reinforced by the later political east–west division of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. The division between these two spheres was enhanced during <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> by a number of events. The <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> collapsed starting the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>. By contrast, the Eastern Roman Empire, mostly known as the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, managed to survive and even to thrive for another 1,000 years. The rise of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Frankish Empire</a> in the west, and in particular the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism</a> that formally divided <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a>, enhanced the cultural and religious distinctiveness between Eastern and Western Europe. Much of Eastern Europe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_occupation_of_Eastern_Europe" title="Mongol occupation of Eastern Europe">was invaded and occupied by the Mongols</a>.</p>
<p>The conquest of the Byzantine Empire, center of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in the 15th century, and the gradual fragmentation of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (which had replaced the Frankish empire) led to a change of the importance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> vs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> concept in Europe. Armour points out that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrillic" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> alphabet use is not a strict determinant for Eastern Europe, where from Croatia to Poland and everywhere in between, the Latin alphabet is used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Greece's status as the cradle of Western civilization and an integral part of the Western world in the political, cultural and economic spheres has led to it being nearly always classified as belonging not to Eastern, but to Southern and/or Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> During the late sixteenth and early seventeenth centuries Eastern Europe enjoyed a relative high standard of living. This period is also called the east-central European golden age of around 1600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interwar_years">Interwar years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Interwar years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A major result of the First World War was the breakup of the Russian, Austro-Hungarian, and Ottoman empires, as well as partial losses to the German Empire. A surge of ethnic nationalism created a series of new states in Eastern Europe, validated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Versailles_Treaty_of_1919" title="Versailles Treaty of 1919">Versailles Treaty of 1919</a>. <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland was reconstituted</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partitions of the 1790s</a> had divided it between Germany, Austria, and Russia. New countries included Finland, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, Ukraine (which was <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ukraine#Ukraine_and_World_Wars" title="History of Ukraine">soon absorbed</a> by the Soviet Union), Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia. Austria and Hungary had much reduced boundaries. Romania, Bulgaria and Albania likewise were independent. All the countries were heavily rural, with little industry and only a few urban centers. Nationalism was the dominant force but most of the countries had ethnic or religious minorities who felt threatened by majority elements. Nearly all became democratic in the 1920s, but all of them (except Czechoslovakia and Finland) gave up democracy during the depression years of the 1930s, in favor of autocratic or strong-man or single party states. The new states were unable to form stable military alliances, and one by one were too weak to stand up against Nazi Germany or the Soviet Union, which took them over between 1938 and 1945.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_the_onset_of_the_Cold_War">World War II and the onset of the Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: World War II and the onset of the Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastern-Europe-small.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="457" data-file-width="414" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Eastern-Europe-small.png/220px-Eastern-Europe-small.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Eastern-Europe-small.png/330px-Eastern-Europe-small.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bc/Eastern-Europe-small.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eastern-Europe-small.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pre-1989 division between the "West" (grey) and "Eastern Bloc" (orange) superimposed on current borders:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CB8807; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Russia (the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federated_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federated Socialist Republic">RSFSR</a>) (dark orange)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EAB34D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other countries formerly part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a> (medium orange)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EEC77F; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Members of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> (light orange)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E9D2A5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other former Communist states not aligned with Moscow (lightest orange)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Russia, defeated in the First World War, lost territory as the Baltics and Poland made good their independence. The region was the main battlefield in the Second World War (1939–45), with German and Soviet armies sweeping back and forth, with millions of Jews killed by the Nazis, and millions of others killed by disease, starvation, and military action, or executed after being deemed as politically dangerous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> During the final stages of World War II the future of Eastern Europe was decided by the overwhelming power of the Soviet Red Army, as it swept the Germans aside. It did not reach Yugoslavia and Albania however. Finland was free but forced to be neutral in the upcoming Cold War. The region fell to Soviet control and Communist governments were imposed. Yugoslavia and Albania had their own Communist regimes. The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> with the onset of the Cold War in 1947 was mostly behind the Western European countries in economic rebuilding and progress. Winston Churchill, in his famous "Sinews of Peace" address of March 5, 1946 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westminster_College,_Missouri" title="Westminster College, Missouri">Westminster College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fulton,_Missouri" title="Fulton, Missouri">Fulton, Missouri</a>, stressed the geopolitical impact of the "iron curtain":</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>From <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Stettin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> an <i>iron curtain</i> has descended across the Continent. Behind that line lie all the capitals of the ancient states of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Eastern Europe. <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Curtain_Final.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1570" data-file-width="1502" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Iron_Curtain_Final.svg/220px-Iron_Curtain_Final.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Iron_Curtain_Final.svg/330px-Iron_Curtain_Final.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Iron_Curtain_Final.svg/440px-Iron_Curtain_Final.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Curtain_Final.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The political borders of Eastern Europe were largely defined by the Cold War from the end of World War II to 1989. The <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> separated the members of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> (in red) from the European members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> (in blue). Dark grey indicates members of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and light grey indicates other neutral countries.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Bloc_during_the_Cold_War_to_1989">Eastern Bloc during the Cold War to 1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Eastern Bloc during the Cold War to 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a></div>
<p>The Soviet secret police, the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a>, working in collaboration with local communists, created secret police forces using leadership trained in Moscow. As soon as the Red Army had expelled the Germans, this new secret police arrived to arrest political enemies according to prepared lists. The national Communists then took power in a normally gradualist manner, backed by the Soviets in many, but not all, cases. They took control of the Interior Ministries, which controlled the local police. They confiscated and redistributed farmland. Next the Soviets and their agents took control of the mass media, especially radio, as well as the education system. Third the communists seized control of or replaced the organizations of civil society, such as church groups, sports, youth groups, trade unions, farmers organizations, and civic organizations. Finally they engaged in large scale ethnic cleansing, moving ethnic minorities far away, often with high loss of life. After a year or two, the communists took control of private businesses and monitored the media and churches. For a while, cooperative non-Communist parties were tolerated. The communists had a natural reservoir of popularity in that they had destroyed Hitler and the Nazi invaders. Their goal was to guarantee long-term working-class solidarity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Eastern Europe after 1945 usually meant all the European countries liberated and then occupied by the Soviet army. It included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" title="German Democratic Republic">German Democratic Republic</a> (also known as East Germany), formed by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone" title="Soviet occupation zone">Soviet occupation zone</a> of Germany. All the countries in Eastern Europe adopted communist modes of control. These countries were officially independent from the Soviet Union, but the practical extent of this independence – except in Yugoslavia, Albania, and to some extent Romania – was quite limited. Under pressure from Stalin these nations rejected grants from the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshall_plan" title="Marshall plan">Marshall plan</a>. Instead they participated in the <a href="/wiki/Molotov_Plan" title="Molotov Plan">Molotov Plan</a> which later evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Comecon" title="Comecon">Comecon (Council for Mutual Economic Assistance)</a>. When <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> was created in 1949, most countries of Eastern Europe became members of the opposing <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, forming a geopolitical concept that became known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a></i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_enlargement.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="691" data-file-width="897" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NATO_enlargement.svg/220px-NATO_enlargement.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NATO_enlargement.svg/330px-NATO_enlargement.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NATO_enlargement.svg/440px-NATO_enlargement.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_enlargement.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Following the disappearance of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> in 1989, the political situation changed and some of the former members of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> gradually joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.

</div>
<ul>
<li>First and foremost was the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (which included the modern-day territories of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>). Other countries dominated by the Soviet Union were the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" title="People's Republic of Poland">People's Republic of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovak Socialist Republic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Hungary" title="People's Republic of Hungary">People's Republic of Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People's Republic of Bulgaria">People's Republic of Bulgaria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Socialist Republic of Romania</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> (SFRY; formed after World War II and before its later dismemberment) was not a member of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. It was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, an organization created in an attempt to avoid being assigned to either the NATO or Warsaw Pact blocs. The movement was demonstratively independent from both the Soviet Union and the Western bloc for most of the Cold War period, allowing Yugoslavia and its other members to act as a business and political mediator between the blocs.</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_People%27s_Republic_of_Albania" title="Socialist People's Republic of Albania">Socialist People's Republic of Albania</a> broke with the Soviet Union in the early 1960s as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a>, aligning itself instead with China. Albania formally left the Warsaw pact in September 1968 after the suppression of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prague_spring" title="Prague spring">Prague spring</a>. When China established diplomatic relations with the United States in 1978, Albania also broke away from China. Albania and especially Yugoslavia were not unanimously appended to the Eastern Bloc, as they were neutral for a large part of the Cold War period.</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1989">Since 1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Since 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">

(dissolved in 1990/1991)<br/>
<span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria"><img alt="Bulgaria" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria_%281971_%E2%80%93_1990%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People's Republic of Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a><br/>

<span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland"><img alt="Poland" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1280" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" title="People's Republic of Poland">Poland</a><br/>
<span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania"><img alt="Romania" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania_%281965-1989%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> in 1989, the political landscape of the Eastern Bloc, and indeed the world, changed. In the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>, the Federal Republic of Germany peacefully absorbed the German Democratic Republic in 1990. In 1991, COMECON, the Warsaw Pact, and the Soviet Union were dissolved. Many European nations which had been part of the Soviet Union regained their independence (<a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltic_States" title="Baltic States">Baltic States</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>). <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">peacefully separated</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> in 1993. Many countries of this region joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, Estonia, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, Latvia, Lithuania, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
